    1129              : /* Convert between RGB and HSB colors, using the hexcone approach (see
    1130              :  * Rogers, David, "Procedureal Elements For Computer Graphics",
    1131              :  * (McGraw-Hill, 1985), pp. 402 - 3).
    1132              :  *
    1133              :  * The rgb ==> hsb calculation is:
    1134              :  *
    1135              :  *   br = max(r, g, b)
    1136              :  *
    1137              :  *   if (br == 0)
    1138              :  *       h = 0, s = 0;
    1139              :  *   else {
    1140              :  *       v = min(r, g, b)
    1141              :  *       diff = br - v;
    1142              :  *       sat = diff / br;
    1143              :  *       if (r == br)
    1144              :  *           h = (g - b) / (6 * diff) + (b > g ? 1 : 0);
    1145              :  *       else if (g == br)
    1146              :  *           h = 1/3 + (b - r) / (6 * diff);
    1147              :  *       else
    1148              :  *           h = 2/3 + (r - g) / (6 * diff);
    1149              :  *   }
    1150              :  */
    1151       166000 : static int rgb2hsb(float *RGB)
    1152              : {

    1154       166000 :     int i, j=0;

    1161          752 :             HSB[2] = RGB[i];

    1163              :         }

    1197              : /* The hsb ==> rgb conversion is:
    1198              :  *
    1199              :  *    mn = (1 - s) * br, md = 6 * s * br;
    1200              :  *
    1201              :  *    switch ((int)floor(6 * h)) {
    1202              :  *      case 0:   %% r >= g >= b
    1203              :  *        r = br;
    1204              :  *        g = mn + h * md;
    1205              :  *        b = mn;
    1206              :  *        break;
    1207              :  *
    1208              :  *      case 1:  %% g >= r >= b
    1209              :  *        r = mn + md * (1/3 - h);
    1210              :  *        g = br;
    1211              :  *        b = mn;
    1212              :  *        break;

    1214              :  *      case 2:  %% g >= b >= r
    1215              :  *        r = mn;
    1216              :  *        g = br;
    1217              :  *        b = mn + (h - 1/3) * md;
    1218              :  *        break;
    1219              :  *
    1220              :  *      case 3:  %% b >= g >= r
    1221              :  *        r = mn;
    1222              :  *        g = mn + (2/3 - h) * md;
    1223              :  *        b = br;
    1224              :  *        break;

    1226              :  *      case 4:  %% b >= r >= g
    1227              :  *        r = mn + (h - 2/3) * md;
    1228              :  *        g = mn;
    1229              :  *        b = br;
    1230              :  *        break;

    1232              :  *      case 5:  %% r >= b >= g
    1233              :  *        r = br;
    1234              :  *        g = mn;
    1235              :  *        b = mn + (1 - h) * md;
    1236              :  *        break;
    1237              :  *
    1238              :  *      case 6:  %% We have wrapped around the hexcone.  Thus this case is
    1239              :  *                         the same as case 0 with h = 0
    1240              :  *        h = 0;
    1241              :  *        r = br;
    1242              :  *        g = mn + h * md = mn;
    1243              :  *        b = mn;
    1244              :  *        break;
    1245              :  *    }
    1246              :  */

    6966              : /*
    6967              :  * The routine which does all the setcolorspace dispatching. This is initially set up by
    6968              :  * zsetcolorspace above. It starts by descending to the bottom-most space
    6969              :  * and setting that as the current space. It then descends the array again
    6970              :  * to the next-to-bottom- space and sets that as the current, and so on.
    6971              :  *
    6972              :  * The 'stage' parameter is passed in to each 'set' method. If a method needs
    6973              :  * to do a continuation itself (eg sample a space) then it should set the stage
    6974              :  * to a non-zero value. When the continuation is complete we return here, and
    6975              :  * attempt to 'set' the same space again. This time stage will be whatever was
    6976              :  * set the first time, which is a signal to the 'set' routine that a continuation
    6977              :  * took place, and is complete. Stage must always be set to 0 when a 'set'
    6978              :  * of a color space is complete.
    6979              :  */
